RATING: 9
Wow. At first glance, I thought that this would NEVER be any good... it just didn't seem "complicated" enough. Boy was I wrong. What a complex gem in such a simple package. It features a terse and simple rule set, there are a few choices each turn, and it has quick game play -- all good things, in my opinion. The key though, is that it has the ability to be a much DEEPER brain-burner than most might think. Certainly a beautiful design if there ever was one.

This is a most wonderful 2-player game.

RATING: 8
As a child I was a big fan of Scotland Yard. I haven't played it for years but this game generates the same feelings of excitement. The pieces are of really good quality, the game plays quick, and the theme is rich. A failure for either player inspires an immediate "one-more-try" feeling, and the fact that it is so quick to play makes this perfectly possible on most occasions. No 2-player game before this one has caused us to play so many games one-after-another in the first few days. Girlfriend is a fan, so this is a big bonus. It's a shame it's only 2-player, but Scotland Yard is still knocking about somewhere so that can scratch the same itch with more players. All in all, very pleased with this purchase.

RATING: 5
2008-08-04

2016-02-24
I would not call Mr. Jack a game of deduction. It is a game of elimination. Let me explain myself... You are not collecting clues and connecting the dots between things that seem to be totally irrelevant at first. Instead, what you do is that every round you are just positioning yourself on the board so that you can eliminate part of the suspects on your list. Inevitably the police will have Jack cornered at some point but the question just is whether they can do it in the time given.

Now we come to the dull part. The basic premise is that the bobs have to eliminate 50% of the remaining suspects every round, and Jack is trying slow the process. For a couple of games this is fun but becomes extremely repetitive after that. There are no alternative strategies, cunning plays or any of that exhilarating excitement from being so close to capturing Jack but then seeing him slip through the net (here I am comparing Mr.Jack with another great game of the same theme: Letters from Whitechapel). 

Nothing is broken with the game. I just did not enjoy it very long.

RATING: 8
I really like this, but you need players to understand the basic setup and strategic goals. E.g. if your opponent doesn't know how to balance escape against staying hidden, how to run with Stealthy from the getgo, or even have a vague idea of how to setup a decoy, even the claimed 70/30 in Inspector's favor is generous to Jack. 

A great idea that is probably needs to be more deduction, less spatial positioning. Random setups, events and less turns would have helped. 

PS agree with Barnes. Turning a guy who disembowelled prostitutes into a cute character is obnoxious.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.4
A game of deduction and elimination which 1 player takes on the role of Mr Jack while the other takes on as the detective on the quest to find which character did Mr Jack impersonate.

With limited number of turns, the detective must be able to deduce the impersonator and move beside the impersonator and expose Mr Jack.  If the character is indeed impersonated, the detective wins the game.

Good points: Easy game to play with and players can take on different roles in the game to have a full taste of the game.

Bad points: Quite hard to remember the different privileges / powers of different characters at first.  The game can be boring if played many times in one go.

RATING: 8.5
Mr. Jack is a "must have" two player game with very little luck and a LOT of strategy.  It plays super quick, with very little down-time.

After 26 plays I'm working out how to best play the role of Jack, which is harder but well worth the effort.

The more I play this game the more clever it becomes.  

The artwork and components are beautiful and the whole game of cat and mouse is wonderfully conceived.  This game is fast approaching 9 plus for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This one stands out because it's so original.  It's nice to have a unique option to go to for a 2 player game.  And each side (Jack and The Detective) is presented with different goals.

Everything is solidly put together, the rules are simple to grasp, but there's a lot of depth in finding the right move.

If I have a complaint it's that the game can really encourage analysis paralysis and take a lot longer than it should.  It's just about possible to map out nearly every reasonable move and weigh them against each other and find the "perfect" move for a turn.  And with that option in reach it's hard to not sit there and try to do it constantly.

But if you can keep that under control, then it's a good game that fills a nice spot.

RATING: 10
Excellent 2 player game. There's a lot of open information on the board, so there's is also some Analysis Paralysis on this game, as you need to plan your moves thoroughly. Each move counts and can be decisive, as each player only plays/moves a character 16 times at max during the whole game. The luck aspect is reduced as you only have to worry about it on the odd turns - 1,3,5 and 7. More experience is needed when playing the role of Jack - as the game isn't perfectly balanced. If you're playing as Mr. Jack and you're Watson you'll have a hard time, because he starts the game in a weak position.
The art work is excelent and add to the quality of the game. Highly recomended!
Sure it's an abstract game, but because each character has it's own especial action he can do, brings the theme more alive, for example: the inspector closes exits, so Mr. Jack can't escape, sherlock holmes can deduce if someone is not guity by drawing alibi cards.
One problem is to visualize your move, sometimes using Goodley, many characters move, it's not easy to visualize the game after the move, and then using your 2nd character movement, and if the 2nd character movement depends on the 1st, you get the ideia...
Play it online at: mrjack.hurricangames.com

RATING: 8
Play as Mr Jack or the detective. Mr Jack is trying to escape the city without getting caught. The detective is trying to figure out who Mr Jack is disguised as and arrest him. What's cool is that the game plays completely differently depending on which role you assume. A clean simple rule set hides the charm of this game: Most of what's going on is happening inside the player's head: 'Does he know who I am? Does he see that I'm heading for the sewers? Did he fall for that ruse?'

Part of it is the play-balance thing (I've never seen Jack win), part of it is the themelessness (almost to the point of negative theme), part of it is that it's just so dry. If I'm going to play an abstract, I'd much rather play a game with real depth like PUNCT or something else from the GIPF series. If I want something with a little bluffing and a little tactics, I'll take Duel in the Dark or Lord of the Rings: The Confrontation. So down the rating goes ...
---
Fun and very clever. It's been billed as a deduction game, which it isn't really, it's more of an abstract tactical game - you do a lot more solving of movement mini-puzzles than actual deduction - but the tactics are quite engaging, and the game has good tension. At least, I think it does - after four games, it feels like it's *very* hard on Mr. Jack. I haven't seen Mr. Jack even close to winning yet, and if the imbalance really is severe, that'll sap the tension. 

The theme is alas a classic euro paste-up job. It's more than a little thematically annoying to be playing the role of Mr. Jack and to never or very rarely be able to actually move your own character, which can happen if the cards come out in an unfriendly order and the inspector always moves him before you get the chance (and let's be clear here, there is a fair amount of luck to this game, and it appears that Jack is especially subject to it). And it's a bit odd to see Sherlock Holmes or Dr Watson actually be Jack the Ripper. I feel like a game on this topic should be a little edgier - how did Jack the Ripper and pirates become acceptable themes for German family-type games?
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4
I'm just not a huge fan of games where you spend a ton of time looking at all the possibilities looking for that one optimal move, and that's a lot of what Mr. Jack boils down to. You can easily win or lose based on one good or bad move, so you have to sit there and look through every possibility until you're satisfied you aren't screwing things up.

Neat game design, but it's just not for me, as I really prefer games where I can play with my gut rather than calculating out every possible move in the game.

RATING: 8
It is a good game of second level deduction, as you have to figure out who Jack is based on the moves the Jack player did or did not make. Implying, of course, that the Jack player will need to make moves that implicate the wrong suspect.

Very nicely done.

However, there are so many movement and placement rules to track, sewers, eight special powers, lights, and adjacency, that new players, and even some forgetful older players, can lose track of this information, giving an enormous advantage to the player that does.

Also, the nature of the Jack crimes (serial killer who murders female sex workers), limits who will be willing to play the game (many of my friends would be uninterested).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Neat little asymmetric two-player game. The deduction comes in the form of clever placement, which is a nice change of pace from Clue variant deduction games.

I find both sides equally fun to play, which is a BIG plus! Also since the play time is so quick, it's easy to play two rounds and switch sides in one sitting.

The problem with this game is the luck factor is pretty high. Mr. Jack, especially if he's disguised as Ms. Stealthy, can win before the other side can do anything meaningful if the right characters come up at the right time. And all too often the game is over before halfway through the turn track just due to luck. Lame.

But, like I said, since it's short and has a unique feel I still dig it overall.

P.S. the art is too cute!

RATING: 7
I held off getting this game both because of its distasteful theme and because it has characters with special powers, which I usually don't like not only because it means more rules to remember, but also because it leads to confusion and often bickering over how different rules interact with each other.  We have the newer printing, which seems to have addressed many of these questions, tacking posts from bgg's faq to the end of the rulebook.  Read the rules and faq carefully and agree on what everything means BEFORE you play.  As for the theme, you can completely ignore it if you like; the game doesn't rely at all on the gruesome details and would work for any mystery theme.  This game can be very close, which is interesting, or someone can win almost immediately, which is rather anti-climatic.  However, the good news in that case is that it didn't take long and you can just play again.  Turns can sometimes drag while someone considers their options, but the game as a whole still plays quickly.  We were expecting the board to be variable set-up after learning the game, but that turned out not to be the case, so we worry this may become somewhat predictable after enough plays.  It has been fine for us so far though.  Most of the character's powers are well thought out to be useful in different situations.  The character tokens are similar to Fearsome Floors'; you have to apply the stickers yourself.  Be especially careful when applying the brown one with the arrow on it.  We didn't realize it would matter, and when we flip the token over (which you do during gameplay) the arrow is facing the wrong way.

RATING: 6
I'm not sure how much of a deduction game this is as opposed to how much of a game it is of finding the clever plays given the current board situation. One player attempts to hide Jack the Ripper, the other to find him.

For the Jack player, this seems to boil down to trying to keep the suspects clustered together in the light, or spread out in the darkness as much as possible, as the detective player uses that as the main way to narrow down the field of suspects.

The main interest here seems to come from the variety of special powers, as each suspect has some ability to bend the rules.

Probably a game that requires equal experience for compelling play, simply because seeing that good move would be easier once one was intimately familiar with the characters and how they can be used.

I don't think I would play it regularly, but a decent little 2 player game.

RATING: 5
OK, so what the hell is the deal with European designers and "cuteing" up subjects like Jack the Ripper?  I mean come on, the titular character is a serial killer that disembowels prostitutes!  Seriously, "Euro-cute" is getting close to the "super deformed" thing from Japan.  I hate it.  Anyway, MR. JACK is a reasonably interesting game that has both a threadbare theme and a threadbare connection to anything approaching the potential greatness that a Jack the Ripper game could offer .  Ripperologists will likely chafe at ahistorical characters like "Miss Stealthy" or the inclusion of Sherlock Holmes (which I thought was kind of cool) but the bottom line is that beyond the title, spare atmosphere, and cutie-pie artwork MR. JACK is really just a lightweight, semi-abstract deduction/bluffing game for two with a reasonable playtime given its depth and mechanics.  The characters (mutually controlled by both players) have fun abilities (the cop blows a whistle and drags characters toward him, Holmes can eliminate suspects) and there's some really interesting ways that the detective player and Ripper player can use the same abilities for entirely different strategies.  The endgame is either pretty brain-burning or a foregone conclusion but for a 30 minute game it's a forgivable sin, I guess.  It's the kind of game where toward the end you usually wind up forced into the One Move You Can Do To Possibly Win or just losing outright.  It's not a bad game at all, but it's thoroughly average on pretty much every count.

RATING: 7.5
Great game that immediately captured me with how clever the design was and how quickly you could play it (big bonus for me ).  A competitive 2 player game that is largely a logic puzzle that combines tactical movement, hidden roles, and logical deduction.
The new artwork is a home-run and does an excellent job of immersing you in the theme of being the paranoid detective leaving a nicotine-laden trail in his search for Jack or being Jack himself and slinking in the shadows looking for the perfect opportunity to slip away just out of the detective's grasp.
Hats off to designer Bruno Cathala, very good game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a surprisingly brain burning game that allows a lot of clever play.  The abilities of the characters are what make the game.  The fact that every other round a player gets to go twice in a row especially adds to the amount of danger present, and allows clever combinations.  Also, the "Jack can't escape when he was seen last round" rule makes choices difficult for Jack and the inspector.  For Jack, is it worth having all of the suspects in the light so the inspector cannot figure out who Jack is, and the reverse for the inspector.  The ability to plan ahead is essential, especially since half the time you know which character cards will be available in the next round, and you have to plan carefully based on the play order.  

All this, and the partner will play it!  What more can I ask for?

Plays:  5

RATING: 8
[2013-02-04 Rating: n.a. -> 8]
Mr Jack is one of my favorite two player games. There's just so much to think about when it's your turn whether you play the Inspector or Mr Jack. But the best thing about it: It has kind of a narrative arc. In the beginning, Mr Jack tries to hide it's identity. Once Mr Jack's identity is discovered, the game can develop into a wild chase.

It's just a lot of fun. The only thing you should be aware of: There is the potential for analysis paralysis since you are confronted with a lot of options each turn.

RATING: 7
Solid two player deduction and movement game.  Eight characters move over a cartoon style game board depicting Whitechapel in the 1880's.  One of the characters is the notorious Mr. Jack, known to the Jack player.  The other player is trying to deduce who Mr. Jack is, and nail him by moving another character to his position to accuse him to win the game.  If Jack can survive eight turns, or move Mr. Jack off the game board - he wins.  Nice simple rules, spiced up by each character having a special power.  First half of the game is deduction (which isn't that hard) and the second half is all about movement and position.  It's a nice two player game, however The Lord of the Rings: The Confrontation has it licked in gameplay.  (Production warning - the Alibi cards tend to "glow" their colour which ruins the game somewhat.  Take a black marker to the edges to disguise them more - you do need to do this!).

RATING: 10
I have a bit of an emotional tie to this game so that gives it a bump in the ratings. Thinking back I remember to when I first bought the game thinking it was expensive at $45 MSRP I think. Then I traded and re-bought which usually means I really like the game. The era of game development that this fits into has passed. One of simpler rules, nice components but not overproduced and an emphasis on accessibility and function. Which is a shame because I'd love to see more games like this than ones that are overwrought with rules and sub-systems. I like that it focuses on a single mechanic (trying to see or not see Jack before he escapes) and just does it exceptionally well.

RATING: 7
This game reminded us of an easy-ish Mastermind.  

The game is slightly more challenging than it originally appears, but the challenge is weighted in favor of the Detective.  That isn't such a horrible thing necessarily as it does add an extra layer of strategy for whoever is playing as Mr Jack to outwit and/or outlast to prevail.  I personally like playing as Mr Jack more for just this reason though I have yet to win. heh

The design of the game is cartoony goodness which I really enjoy, and I appreciate that they added stickers for the people tokens on the board rather than just plain old wooden colors.  It really helps you get into the world of Mr Jack.

Because of the character design and challenge of playing as Mr Jack, I'll play this game on a semi-regular basis.  It's a good quickie before you move on to a more serious title later in the evening.

RATING: 6

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
One player is the Detective, and the other player is Jack the Ripper. There are 8 characters on the board. One of them is Jack, but his identity is unknown to the Detective. Both players have partial control over all the characters. To win, the Detective must accuse Jack within 8 turns. In order to do this, he must correctly deduce Jack's identity, then get another character to Jack's location. Jack wins if he escapes the city, if he remains unaccused after 8 turns, or if the Detective falsely accuses the wrong character. Jack may only escape if he was not witnessed on the previous turn. Through control of the characters available, their positions, the careful movement of street lamps, manhole covers, and roadblocks, the players play a cat-and-mouse game of risk, bluffing, and wit.

[url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/218547]SEE MY REVIEW[/url]

RATING: 7
Ingenious game of cat & mouse where the light is at times your shield or your curse.  To escape, Jack has to be invisible; to lower your chances of exposure, you have to try to stay in the light with as many other suspects as possible.  Therein lies the challenge, when and how to break free.  My two complaints about the game is that for Jack to escape, a fair measure of luck is required in the available characters when the opportunity would be there, and for Jack to outlast exposure, there is no reason for the investigator not to take a gamble to expose him.  At that point the odds depend on the number of unconfirmed suspects.  We find the ending anticlimatic when it comes down to a gamble.  The rest of the game though has a great feeling and packs a whole lot of tension for such a minimalist design.

RATING: 4
Finally played for the first time as both Jack and the investigator.

Somewhat interesting, but I'm struggling to get the strategy.  Since the various characters are usually always within 3 of another character, you really need, as Jack, to wait until the odd turns where the Jack character is not available for your use.  You want to use the other characters to move away from Jack so that he is not seen, and then on the even turn where you go first, you can move him out.

That also means that Jack needs to hug an exit.

In both games I played, Jack was known within 3 turns, but was able to escape because when he was discovered he was already next to an exit and Jack moved first the next turn.

Not a fan of the slightly cartoony artwork.  Would have preferred something a little more realistic.

Jury is out on this until I know how to correctly play both roles.

UPDATE: of course I forgot that Jack could wait out the inspector, so now it becomes a little easier as Jack since you could try to clump things up so that everyone is near everyone else.

Downgraded to 4 since I think things are still slanted in the Inspectors favor, although I don't feel there are multiple paths to victory for Jack, and really only 1-2 ways to play him.

RATING: 9
It has been said a lot that this game feels like mastermind. I beg to disagree. The deduction part is so simple that the game is mostly one of forcing your opponent to place the pieces in a configuration that is optimal for you. Therefore to me, that game feels more like an abstract movement game than a deduction game. That being said it is a truly excellent movement game, and the theme meshes in quite well. You can try a lot of different tactics: to bluff your opponent, to setup a complex position, to block some pieces... The assymetry is well-balanced and it is really fun and challenging to play on either side. Thanks to Hurrican for the brilliant idea of taking this micro-edited game and bringing it to a wider audience.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Truly an excellent game design that is based on one of the most infamous serial murder sprees in recorded history.

The White Chapel Murders exemplifies the maxim that truth is stranger than fiction, and actual horror can be just as revulsive as anything imagined.

Look at the pictures of the butchered victims of the "Ripper" if you doubt this veracity.

Dracula by Kosmos is an excellent 2 player, deductive game with a dark theme. But Dracula is fictitious, and so are his victims. The women who were disected by the the White Chapel killer were real people. If this game was called "Mr. Jeffrey" (Jeffrey Dahmer) or "Mr. Richard" (Richard Speck) would the game enjoy the popularity of Mr. Jack? Remember, the attitude of Mr. Jack is comedic...the images of the characters, real and fictitious, are a burlesque, they are mere caricatures of the people represented; the effect of this treatment of the theme is a trivialization of the historical event.

There is a line that some gamers feel uncomfortable crossing. Mr. Jack, IMO, crosses that line.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
This is an excellent 2 plater deduction game. Loads of fun for gamers to families. It may take a few plays to pick up on some of the startegies in the game. Also, I can see some people may have issues with AP, but that should pick up with a few plays and not be to bad of a problem.

The game looks great and the components are very well made. With big thick cards, wooden tokens and a nicely detailed game board. If your still unsure about the game. You can try it online for free at hurricane games.com

Many thanks to my friends Raimond and Mats, for introducing and getting me hooked on this game. I love it.

RATING: 7
Mr. Jack is a 2 player game in which one of the players is the Detective and the other is Jack the Ripper.

This medium/light game takes about 40 minutes of play and has a set of very simple yet deep rules.

The goal of the detective is to uncover the identity of Mr. Jack and the goal of Jack is to either escape from the game board or to not be uncovered in the game‚Äôs 8 turns.

For 2 players.
Ages 9 and up.
Playing time: 30 to 45 minutes.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Mr. Jack is a cute but intense tactical puzzle game of bluff, positioning, and lookahead.  It's not really a "deduction" game.  It's a game of "if I do this, then she'll have to do that, leaving me with this move, unless she knows that this character is innocent, in which case . . . ."  The interaction of the characters' abilities and the lamps and the sewers and the turn order and the adjacency rule creates some wonderfully complex situations.

Unfortunately, Jack faces long odds if the detective plays flawlessly.  Fortunately, achieving flawless play as the detective is damn hard.  The game's enthralling even if Jack is usually caught.  As Jack, if you can force the detective to make a 50/50 guess at the end, you're doing a good job.  If you can subtly bluff him so that he chooses the wrong suspect, then you're doing an outstanding job.

The "Jack flees the board" victory condition is like the temple connection win in Attika.  A good player can almost always prevent it if he devotes enough attention, but doing so will slow down his investigation, buying Jack time.  The threat of escape is crucial to the game, even if it never actually happens.

RATING: 9
Wow!  Great 2-player game.  Played 6 times in a row with the wife.  Great tension and quick play.  Best 2-player game out there.  Easy to learn and deceptively tactical play.

Although the rules are simple, there can be several difficult descisons to be made per round.  Do not play this game with people prone to "analysis by paralysis".  A quick 15 minute game can turn into a 45 minute borefest.  I played with a buddy of mine who plays poker a lot and the game went forever.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Chess like brain-burner of a game. There are very few moves that make up a game of Mr. Jack (you will pick and move 16 characters through the course of an entire game, IF you play the full 8 rounds). But there are SO many possibilities for your moves. I don't like how intensely you need to concentrate. I don't like how you must think through the consequences of an entire round before making your first move; its almost like both players sit for 10 minutes when a round starts thinking about all the possible outcomes and then you spend 60 seconds grabbing and moving the 4 characters around. 

So what is good then? I love the challenge of escaping (much harder for Jack to win, especially when new to the game). There is LOTS of room for some sneaky, clever plays. This one rewards repeated play as there is so much information to consider when making your moves. I love the subtle deduction that goes on (if Sherlock was Mr. Jack why did he move here instead of here? But is that to make me think Lestrade is Mr. Jack? etc.). I like how some seemingly insignificant plays can have a big impact if you come up with a good strategic play.

All in all, not fantastic, but fun and a keeper. I will play from time to time. Mostly, though, if I have a partner willing have a drink and a conversation over a slow thinking man's (or woman's) game.

RATING: 9
Excellent marriage of gameplay and theme (okay, the subject is a bit morbid, but if you like, imagine that Jack just ripped the "do not remove" tags off of mattresses... it doesn't really matter what he did in terms of the gameplay), and a very creative new kind of mystery game. Others have described it as a combination of chess and Clue, and I think that's very apt. Like most games, it took me a game or two of "what??" before it all fell into place as to what I was supposed to be doing. At that point, a game can go a few directions for me; "Ah, okay, now I get it... Let's play something else now." or "Ah, okay, now I get it... We'll have to play that again sometime." or "Ah, okay, now I get it... Let's play that again!"  This was definitely in the latter category for me, and I immediately created several games right away at http://mrjack.biludi.de/ and I'm now waiting for the box version to arrive. For something that seems so simple and is set up the same way every game, it can play out a remarkable number of ways. A brilliant and very clever design and a really fun game!

RATING: 9
Great game. I love this game. A combination of strategic positioning and deduction skills; like Chess meets Clue.

Light enough to pick up and play quickly, but complex enough to require some real decision-making. Random elements add just a small bit of luck but greatly increase replayability.  Definitely a little tougher for the Mr. Jack player, but that works well if you have a more advanced gamer who could use a slight handicap.

Certain winning conditions (such as escape) are very difficult, but keep things interesting.

Probably my favorite 2-player game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
This is a really great short two player euro game.  It can be a little bit of a brain burner, as you consider the different possible moves each person might take under different circumstances to figure out what you can do to best improve your position.  It reminds me of an abstract game in that regard, but the theme here is very strong.  The special powers and the "terrain" are very thematic.  I haven't played enough to know if it is balanced for jack vs. good guys, BUT its so short that if it was unbalanced you could each play both sides.  There aren't that many great short deep 2 player euros --- this game fills a pretty unique niche, and it fills it well!

RATING: 6
A quick playing game of strategy and deduction.  One player tries to eliminate suspects, while the other tries to move the pieces to make the first player's task more difficult.

Game pieces are of excellent quality!  There was a problem when they cut the cards as the card's color is visible on the sides (a bad thing).  They suggest placing the deck in the box so the side is not visible.  This solution works quite well.

RATING: 4
I think I might be in the minority for this rating, but hear me out. I personally feel this game is really skewed in the detective's favor. Within the first round or so the detective has already eliminated half of the 8 suspects. I understand this is supposed to feel like a cat and mouse chase, but I feel that both players should really have equal chance of winning. Now after more plays, my opinion may change, but for now, it might be a little while before I try to bring this to the table again. I personally feel this is a game you should try to get on sale if you're interested. I don't think I would feel so burned if I had waited to get it on sale.

RATING: 6
First played August 23rd, 2007.  This is a quick learn <5min) and a medium quick play (30min) as a two player game.  One player plays Mr. Jack and tries to escape and the other plays the policeman and tries to catch Mr. Jack.  It looked too simple to be true.  I thought that it would be pretty easy to capture Mr. Jack (who I played) however once we got into it, I realized that it can be a bit more tricky to figure out.  It reminded me a bit of Scotland yard, however for two people.  I liked it enough to play it again to see if my initial thoughs were correct, however I don't know if I'll play it beyond the 2nd play with so many other choices out there.  It does have a good mix of luck and strategy for what the game is.

RATING: 8
This game .. great!
I had to admit i was a bit sceptic, but it all worked out fine. 
Its a great game. Some games they give a name and when you play the game you think... why did they name the game that way? Its just.. another cardplay.. with a name that is not realy related to the game at all. ( the feeling i had when i played Spy, it sounded very interesting, but once you played it .. just another card game in wich you have to collect cards...)
But with this game its different. When you play this game you can realy put yourself in your role. You as Mr jack trying to escape! or as the inspector tryin kick his ass!  I think this is a great game. I prefer boardgames over card games and me and my boyfriend where always looking for a nice game for the 2 of us.. And with this, we found one!

2 Player
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Very good unique little bluffing game that is themed quite well (read theme works together with mechanics nicely), no reason to play Clue ever again howver Clue utilizes deduction where as here it barely exists as this is more based on the process of elimination and puzzle solving (well I guess Clue is also the process of elimination).  

Elimination is exactly what you are trying to do as the detectives and exactly what you want to prevent if your Jack.  This means it becomes a tactical game of manoeuvring where the detective's job is to try to separate the characters into two equal groups so the max number can be eliminated, Jacks job is to stop this of course. One of the best parts of the game I think is how Jack can bluff the detective by a clever move at the right time leading to a planned 'mis-direction' which can even win Jack the game. 

Mostly tactical but neat tactics, outstanding components, chaotic which is a little unusual for a 2 player game, strategy mostly obvious and even more so for detectives but some decent choices to be made with the characters and their accompanying powers and a little planning to be had as well. I like the diminishing lights, movable barrides and movable manhole covers and the movement option the manholes provide, all neat stuff.

Nice short playtime makes this a great filler for two for weeknights

[u]UPDATE:[/u] 7 => 7.5 Really a great two player game and an especially good couples game, very easy to pick up and play as there are no cumbersome rules and always FUN to play. So far the best game I've played by any designers named Bruno...

RATING: 4

UPDATE: Bumped my rating down to a 4 because last time someone suggested playing it I actively campaigned for something else.  I can see why people like it, but I don't enjoy it at all...

RATING: 7.5
Two-player game featuring eight suspects wandering around the Whitechapel district, one of whom is really Jack the Ripper trying to escape the area before being caught. One player knows the identity of Jack, the other player tries to discover his identity and then catch him.

Having played a few times, I find the game quite enjoyable. It plays quickly, there is a lot to think about, and the artwork is nice (if a bit out of character for so grim a theme). I can't really conclude anything about game balance yet, but my games all ended with fast and convincing detective victories, which makes me worry that perhaps balance isn't quite right. Still, a nice if not overwhelmingly marvellous game.

Initial Rating: 7.0 (March 2012)

Mr. Jack is a good game. The components and gameplay are very nice. You can explain the game under 10 minutes and play it under 30 minutes, still it is deep enough leaving me with a satisfying feeling after finishing it. Due to this, the game lends itself to multiple consecutive plays, almost always, we play this twice in a row but exchanging roles. Also, we often comment what mistakes or what plays we did during the game. Good stuff.
 
It has some luck of the draw with the characters and Sherlock¬¥s power and this bothers me a bit, but as the game plays so quickly I don‚Äôt mind much. I‚Äôm concerned about the game balance, in most of my games, the Jack player has lost and when I play Jack, I feel I have a lot less control. I¬¥m also concerned about replayability (thus the rating), so I bought the expansion to keep things different every play. 

For now, I plan to play this again soon.

Current Rating: 6.0
[hr]
2014-05-06

I still haven‚Äôt played with the expansion because I feel the base game still has a lot to offer. The replayability is no longer an issue for me, every game feels different and the decisions are not obvious.

My opinion of Mr. Jack continues to improve. It is true than winning as Jack is harder, but it is possible and VERY satisfying.

I will continue to play Mr. Jack in the near future and perhaps its rating will continue to rise.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
What is all the hype about this game?  The deduction is the rawest form of binary splitting... and the detective player should have no trouble figuring our who Jack is within 3 or 4 turns, max.

The rest of the game is all in the luck of the draw... Jack draws the right cards and avoids capture, he wins.  If the detective player can get the larger movement characters he can close on Jack and win himself... might as well flip a coin when Jack is discovered.

I own most of the Kosmos two-player line and, as a two-player game, Mr. Jack is inferior to nearly all of them.  There is just no fun here.

Regardless of play, Mr. Jack is definitely not worth its suggested list price... and probably not worth playing more than one or two times.

LAST PLAY: 2010
[/color][color=blue]
Interesting deduction game.

One player is Mr Jack and the other one is the detective, trying to discover which of the 8 different characters is Mr Jack.

Each turn players put the candidates in light or in shadow, the detective trying to eliminate some candidates and Mr Jack trying to confuse his opponent and escape. Each character has a special power that can be used to help the players.

Good one, very different to other games.[/color]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
The wife and I absolutely love Letters from Whitechapel, but it is rather involved and takes a while to complete (plus, we like it better as a game for more than 2 people, anyhow). So, for these reasons, we were in the market for a somewhat lighter and possibly quicker 2 player game that might be similar to LfW. I picked up Mr. Jack because of the similarity in theme and on the game shop owner' recommendation/testament to its popularity.  Unfortunately, after a few playthroughs we remain unimpressed.  For one, it dones't seem to have as much deduction strategy involved as we had hoped for.  Regardless of what you do as the detective, the options for suspects are narrowed down significantly and independently of your actions in the first portion of the game, which just seems wasteful.  Yes, the strategy does become more important throughout the rest of the game, increasingly so, however, it feels like the game is doing a lot of the mechanic for you in this regard.  For example, the pieces and suspects are all placed onto the gameboard in the same spots everytime, never varying.  It feels very inflexible for strategy buffs like us.  
The art is good, but the game board is pretty darn small, which provides the players -- especially Jack, with not as many options as you would like to have available to you.  Whereas London feels huge in LfW, Mr. Jack makes London feel like a city block surrounded by a wall.  

I'll be honest and say that we still need to give it a chance and play it for what it is rather than judge it against what it's not (LfW), but for now, this is going on the "meh" list. 

Oh, one more thing, since the tone is much more cartoonish and playful in Mr. Jack, I could see this being a great game for a family with young kids or teenagers.  THe strategies involved are basic enough for them to get down well and the theme is suitable, as opposed to the much more macabre feeling of LfW.

RATING: 7
Initally was not impressed when I opened the box and one play. There wasn't much; eight character tokens, alibi cards, character cards, a witness card, turn marker and board. The game does get better with more plays. You really have to know how to play the different character advantages and really know your movement options durring play (the manholes) this game becomes really challenging. It starts off as a cat-in-mouse game with trying to confuse the inspector then it is an 'escape' out of town. It seems like a really simple game but it is fun playing Jack or the inspector. Overall - I like this game. I really think my wife will enjoy this game (which is why i wanted the game in the first place).

RATING: 10
A great deduction game for 2-players where neither player needs to write anything down. The game offers interesting decisions for character movement by incorporating semi-random character availability and special powers. I find this combination to be a perfect balance of strategy and luck.

Many have criticized the game as favoring the inspector. Am I the only one who prefers to play as Mr Jack? As Jack, I have won far more games than lost. Two of those losses were 50-50 shots in the 8th round. Thus, I consider them moral victories!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Right about when we started learning about boardgames, [GAMEID=21763] started getting a lot of buzz.  Plus, it seemed like it would be similar to [GAMEID=1294], which she really liked but didn't work for two players.

Unfortunately, we are probably in the minority, but it didn't really work for us.  Part of the problem was one of expectations.  We were anticipating a game like [GAMEID=1294], where it would be mostly deduction-based.  And that is part of the game, since the detective player does need to identify the secret identify of Mr. Jack.  However, in practice [GAMEID=21763] played more like a tactical, positional game almost more similar to an abstract game like [GAMEID=2083] than to [GAMEID=1294].  It's a deceptively analytical, brain-burning game.  It's also a very reactionary game---it's hard to develop any long term strategies, since the useable characters are shared by the two players and they vary randomly every two rounds.  And while each of the characters does have a special ability, some of them seem much stronger than the others and it takes a lot of experience to be able to use the more subtle characters effectively.  All in all, it was definitely a lot more brain burn-y that we thought it would be.  

Also, it took a long time for either one of us to win as Jack, which also didn't help.  Most games ended up with Jack getting caught or getting to the end with basically a coin flip decision.

It's one of those games that I can appreciate, but probably will rarely hit the table due to the mental energy involved.  Most nights, by the time we get home, we're just too exhausted to play something this involved.

Simple, but not banal. Quick.
Fine artwork.

UPDATE (rating downgraded from 7 to 6): Jack's chances to flee are so slim that his best choice is to keep two characters always suspected (more likely both enlighteed) to force a random accusation in the last turn, effectively turning the game into an elaborated maneuvering to decide the winner with a coin flip. Dissatisfying.

RATING: 4
Although this is a pleasantly quick and reasonably interesting bluffing game for two, there is such a severe disconnect between the theme and its presentation that I felt quite a bit uncomfortable while playing it. Whether the Whitehall murders are a good subject for any game is debatable, but using this horrible piece of history for a very light game seems tasteless, especially when the aim for one player is to have ‚ÄòJack‚Äô successfully escape the law. Whimsical illustrations and a couple of fictional characters push it further into what-were-they-thinking territory for me.

The strangest thing about this is that the theme is so abstracted that the (quite solid) mechanics could easily have been transferred to a more appropriate subject. As things are, I‚Äôll avoid playing this and just shake my head in disbelief every time I read that people think of this as a great game for children.

RATING: 7

RATING: 8
It's interesting how your taste in games evolves over the years. That evolution, admittedly, is not linear. That is, it doesn't necessity progress in a consistent fashion. There are ebbs and flows. Ticket to Ride, Carcassonne, Dominion--these are some of the gateway games that brought me into the hobby, but very soon, I tired of playing them and looked to slightly more advanced fare (Stone Age, Vikings, Kingsburg), and then Puetro Rico and Caylus, etc. But what's so investing is how your feelings about games wane over time, how they seem to change almost regularly. Well, mine do anyway, and I'm in a phase right now where I enjoy lighter games--or at least light-medium. As a 2 player, Mr. Jack fits the bill quite nicely. The reason for the aforementioned explanation is this: we played Mr. Jack for the first time about 2 years ago, didn't care for it, and traded it soon after. It was just sort of "meh" at the time. I was interested in the changes in the 2016 edition so I investigated it as much as possible. You see, Mr. Jack is a game I really want to like. I love the theme (history teacher), the art, the fact that it's 2 player, etc. So, I was a bit disheartened that the game was a flop the first time. I CAN TELL YOU THOUGH, the new edition seems to be a whole different game. I'm not sure if my tastes have waned again, and that's all it is, or if this game has seen a massive overhaul. I think it might be a bit of both, because this game is awesome! The one nitpick I have is the fact that the "innocent cards" are printed a bit off-center in my copy, creating some inconsistencies between it and the expansion. That aside, I can't recommend Mr. Jack highly enough. Simple, beautiful, compelling and it only takes about a half hour of your time.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

RATING: 7
It's a good gateway into cat and mouse style deduction games. As a middle of the road game, it gives a little taste of many different elements. Its quick and easy gameplay allow gamers to asses their enjoyment in what they did or did not like about it, which they can then use to maybe find another more niche deduction game that's more closely tailored to their likes. Did they like or dislike the character powers? Did they like the length of play? Do they want a tougher brain burning scenario? I found that these questions helped lead me to other great games such as Specter Ops, Letters from Whitechapel, Fury of Dracula, and Sleuth. In addition, i love Mr Jack's theme, and its artwork is done in a cute cartooney way that makes this game accessible to everyone.

RATING: 6
Beautiful 2-player board game where one person is the inspector and the other is Jack the Ripper. 
 Players take turns moving a collective group of suspects, each with unique abilities, around the board. The Inspector is trying to figure out which citizen Jack the Ripper actually is by strategically organizing the citizens into groups in a process of suspect elimination while Jack tries to keep things as un-enlightening as possible for the inspector in hopes of either escaping when no witnesses are around or after the 8th round of investigation. 
 A fun enough game, but biased towards the investigator's success, which is a bit of a deterrent for me to want to play this game often.

RATING: 5.5
Game in a Nutshell: Players work to either expose or hide the identity of Mr Jack through role selection and processes of elimination.

Two-player only.

Pros: Good mix of deduction, bluffing, role-selection, and strategic positioning. Simple to learn, but there's still plenty under the surface. Excellent, sturdy components should hold up to repeated play. Satisfying ending where Jack either gets away or is caught as opposed to counting points.

Cons: Enough to think about that the game could drag on longer then it needs to. All the added mechanics might be too much for a casual non-gamer to enjoy a surface-simple deduction game.

Other: One game has left me feeling like I have plenty to learn here. 

Best Use: The best two-player deduction game out there at a medium weight.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Possibly the most enjoyable two player game I have played. While the gameplay takes some liberties (why are Jack and the detective moving the same characters?), the game as a whole (the artwork, the characters, the game of cat and mouse) does a great job of conjuring up the theme. Despite the special rules for each character, it's not very complicated and moves very smoothly.

It can be frustrating: You can try to plan ahead, but you'll have to make do with the cards you get and your opponent will probably screw up your plans!

RATING: 7
Is quickly becoming my favourite 2 player game. Has the exact right length, allows for multiple plays in a row while remaining fun, and the ever-changing card order ensures different gameplay each time. Jack as a hard time though - even if you play (near) "perfectly" and do not try to escape, your opponents Holmes' card  from a few turns back may hand him the game. For now, I don't think it's a huge problem though, and I will keep enjoying Mr. Jack for it's deceptive plays, and the myriad ways of manipulating your opponent's mind....
In fact, the only problem with the game I foresee is the fixed setup, and the fixed characters; perhaps leading to repetitive openings and/or a stale game experience over time. I therefore look forward to trying the extension / expansion should that moment arrive.

RATING: 8
2-player deduction game where Jack is trying to escape or last 8-rounds without being caught.  There are 8 different suspects and after each round Jack must explain whether he is "in the light" or "in the dark". RATING: 8
Played once. This is a two player game where one player is trying to secretly get one of the eight characters on the board off of the map, while the other player is trying to figure out which character the other player is trying to get off of the map. Each character on the board has special powers, and only four of them may be moved each round.

This game has neat mechanics, and is amazingly stressful (yet fun) to play. I look forward to many more games :-)

RATING: 7
A two player game, where one player is Jack the Ripper (Mr. Jack), while the other player is the detective. There are 8 different characters on the board, and Mr. Jack is one of them, attempting to flee the board. The detective tries to deduce who is Mr. Jack. Each of the characters has special abilities. Each turn, Mr. Jack declares if he is "seen" (beside a lamp or adjacent to another character) or "unseen". From this, the detective can try to deduce who Mr. Jack is, and the game ends in a maximum of 8 turns. This is a fun game, easy to play, and is fairly quick. However, it is very difficult for Mr. Jack!

RATING: 7
Man, this game made my brain hurt! I don't think I'm usually susceptible to "analysis paralysis" but I definitely succumbed to it here. 

The game consists of 8 characters, each with a certain ability, one of whom is Jack the Ripper. The "Jack" player must try to keep Jack's identity hidden while trying to maneuver Jack off of the game board; meanwhile, the "Inspector" player is trying to determine which character is Jack and be able to capture him before the end of 8 rounds. Players take turns moving 1 of 4 available characters each turn, alternating 1, 2, 1 characters.

There is so much to keep in mind on your turn with this game: what characters are available to move, which will/may be available next turn, what abilities will help you or your opponent. Of course, the plan to you form can be quickly destroyed by your opponent's move.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
As far as detective games are concerned, Mr. Jack is a one-of-a-kind: instead of asking question after question until reaching a conclusion, this quick, tactical and cut-throat duel between Jack the Ripper and the inspector requires both players to move the eight pieces on the board (seven authentic roles and one usurped by Jack, each with its own special ability) once each turn before Jack says if there are "witnesses" or not (i.e. if he's next to another piece or to a street lamp currently working). Jack will win if the keeps hidden for eight turns or if he avoids the police cordons and quits the scene.

Mr. Jack is a deduction game where deduction itself is the end rather than the means: the amount of information disclosed every round will depend on the positioning of the pieces on the board - positioning the pieces to squeeze or deny as much information as possible is actually what constitutes the biggest challenge in the game. The way characters are drafted to be moved brings a healthy dose of luck but players can still use each move very differently (even by choosing the characters in different order). 

The learning curve of the game is clearly steeper for the Jack player.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Great deduction and bluff for 2-players: traditionally the hardest number to make this genre of game work. A very rough ride if you're playing Jack, and therefore a little frustrating, but the production values are excellent (perhaps a little TOO good for an otherwise swift game) and there is plenty of repeatability in playing it both ways.

RATING: 8
It's a favorite theme of mine and I was also attracted by the game award nominations and postive comments on BGG. 

"Mr Jack" is a good 2-player match-of-wits. Not deep, but clever, it's a good example of a game that's well thought-out and does not pretend to be more than what it actually is. 

Still would love to see a 'Jack the Ripper' game that is more thematic and more based on the actual history (perhaps one already exists and I'm just not aware of it), even though with its characters and how they affect play there is certainly theme to be found in the game. 

Purchased September 2008. My son Trevor rated it a 9 as of October of 2009 (when he was 10 1/2). Raised my rating to an 8 in July of 2012, because every time I play this game I love doing so.

WARNING: Bevelled edges on character cards have been cut from the wrong side, meaning the coloured backgrounds are slightly visible from the side when stacked together. RATING: 6
It's a good game but I don't like this kind of games.

I share Mr. Houjix's opinion: [q]Mr. Jack disappoints me. I love the idea of a quick game of deduction and bluff. That may be what Mr. Jack is billed as, but it certainly isn't what the game actually is. Under the hood this is just a mediocre [not my opinion] tactical maneuvering game with zero deduction and almost zero bluff in it. In fact, Mr. Jack is most closely related to games like Chess and Hive. It's about processing tactical permutations. I really dislike those sorts of games. [‚Ä¶] I can appreciate the uniqueness of the design but the gameplay is lacking for me, and that bums me out. For a short two player game of tactics and double guess Lord of the Rings: the Confrontation [‚Ä¶] is vastly superior.[/q]

RATING: 5
Seems like a whole lot of to-do over not-much. There just isn't much compelling to this game - same layout each time, then first turn you get to move 2 people and that reveals a whole bunch. Then subsequent rounds have less and less to cover. Seems many plays boil down to a quick escape by Jack if he isn't totally bottled up tight. Anticlimactic as all get out. Most importantly, this is not a thief/hunter game - this is a puzzle game, which may explain why so many people like it. I find it very fiddly, a terrible learning curve (i.e. it takes many many plays to become proficient with the Jack strategies) and a bad gateway game, as well as bad for children.

RATING: 2
this game has a cool flavor, despite the presence of some ahistorical characters in the game. that said, this game's premise promises more than the gameplay actually manages to deliver. i really like the movement and the variable powers of the various characters. i feel like these help create the opportunity for some clever play. unfortunately, i feel like the ability to only move characters whose cards come up severely hampers the player playing jack the ripper. sometimes, due to the game opening position of the characters, and the luck of the draw, the jack the ripper player will have a rough time defensively positioning himself and not throwing the game to the investigator player. actually, this is true for every turn of the game. 

so basically, the whole game rests on flawless play by the ripper player, and the luck of the draw as far as what character cards come up. i fail to see the challenge for the investigator player at all. the investigator player can play suboptimaly for most of the game and still win, whenever the ripper character makes a mistake, or when the cards limit the ripper's defensive ability too much. i feel like a much more satisfying two player deduction game would be scotland yard.     

update: man this game is terrible.  there's barely a game here.

RATING: 8
Very clever 2-player puzzle/detective game full of "aha" moments!

Beginners think it's terribly hard to win with Jack, but that's false.  The game is pretty balanced once you know what you're doing.  (See the [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/261489]strategy article[/url] by FerrumEtBombyx.)  Newbies make mistakes like trying too hard to escape with Jack instead of keeping all the suspects together and visible.

The only real downside is that often the detective must guess between the remaining suspects in the end, so all the cleverness by both players can come down to a matter of a lucky/unlucky guess.

But sometimes Jack can arrange things so that in the final turn the Detective knows for sure who Jack is, but can't reach him to accuse him - leading to delightful wails of anguish from the Detective player!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
An excellently designed and executed game with good components.  Quick and tense, my 13-year-old son likes to play very much.  A two-person version of "Clue" that works; it has tension, mystery, luck, deduction, and a feeling of options slowly narrowing down.  I agree it is harder to play the "Jack" side, but I find that bluffing is the best way to outwit the detective.

RATING: 4

Disappointing. A quotation of Reiner Knizia comes to mind, whereby the last twenty percent of game design are the really hard work. Obviously Bruno and Ludovic did not spend too much energy beyond those 80 % to save a nice basic idea.  In short: the imbalance between the two roles makes this game really pointless.

Surely you could turn this into a really good game by introducing clever house rules, f.e. a scoring mechanism for consecutive games, rewarding Mr. Jack with (not linear) increasing points for each round he doesn't get caught etc. But I prefer games that work fine without self-made improvements. thoia's comment (see below) says it all. Vastly overrated!

RATING: 7
I really anticipated playing this, but it fell flat for me. Too much thinking for a 20-minute game, and I felt like I was arbitrarily moving pieces around according to arbitrary movement rules. Really hard to wrap up all the possibilities, and a complete brain workout. The brain-burn involved seems so much denser when you compress it to 20 minutes of game time. 

---------------------

I'm still not liking Mr. Jack right now, but I'd play it against somebody who doesn't over-analyze, because it's quick and pretty with a good theme. Definitely a game that emphasizes thinking on your feet (the moment the character cards are revealed at the start of the turn).

-------------------

After my 4th play, I understand the game and like it now. This game might sell itself as a deduction game, but the dominating part of it is actually abstract strategy. There is deduction involved in Jack's bluffing and the detective's picking up on tiny movements and inadvertent comments. But to do well in the game, it's all in the character drafts. You want to leave your opponent with the fewest options possible, while properly handling the spatial elements on the board. That's the very essence of abstract strategy. 

The asymmetry is very well done. Jack can only escape when he is not witnessed, but it's easier to keep Jack in the light. This buys the detective time, and gives him the option of narrowing down the investigation or ensuring that Jack cannot escape by witnessing all suspects. But as time goes on, it gets progressively easier for Jack to slink into the shadows as the lamps start turning off.

There are a lot of games which are inherently abstract mechanically, but get ruined because of a completely unnecessary theme that doesn't fit at all. But Mr. Jack is the rare abstract strategy game where the whodunnit investigation theme makes the game more enjoyable and satisfying. In contrast, Mystery Rummy - Jack the Ripper hurts its own gameplay with its theme.

==============

theory described it best.

[q]Mr. Jack is a game that:

1) masquerades as a deduction game
2) is actually more of a spatial reasoning game
3) until you both become very good at it, at which point it returns to a deduction game [/q]
I got to (2) on 3rd play, just started realizing 3) during 5th play.

Some interesting dynamics from's Mr. Jack perspective:

1. Getting a large number of people eliminated early isn't bad at all, and might even be better. With many, there's the risk that the Detective just gets lucky and finds Mr. Jack in the smaller (maybe only 1) group, but with few, it's easier for you to choose who to protect.
2. Do not go for escape unless you can guarantee it with your character definitely coming out next turn, and you going first (even then, it's difficult because Detective gets last move right before). Nothing's worse than having 2-3 characters able to escape, but not doing so, and letting the Detective know who isn't Mr. Jack. Corollary: might want to keep people in the light after all (which is easier anyway) and go for the shadows only when trying to escape.
3. Each character has 2 states to track: position and status (light/shadow). Characters on display will change their position. Status can usually be changed for anybody, especially shadow -> light. Sergeant (and to a lesser extent, the master of disguise) is the only character that can change other characters' positions, which makes him the most powerful, in my opinion.

4+3

RATING: 8
[9 plays] This is extremely well done. Gameplay is fun, can make your head hurt deliciously, and is very straightforward. Rules are great, components are excellent, and the artwork is nice. Definitely the best 2 player deduction game I have ever played.

After playing several times, here are my initial impressions:
* Jack is at a slight disadvantage, perhaps 70/30 as others have said, but I don't mind that kind of challenge a bit.
* Escape should rarely be the primary goal for Jack, concealing information for as long as possible is the highest priority - escape is a crime of opportunity, particularly if you can set it up in the second half of the game.
 
Most recent play 11-1-08 with Garrett.

RATING: 7
Tried to get it from Neuroludic...sold out. This 2-player game sees one player as a detective and the other as Jack the Ripper. Jack is trying to elude capture by turn 8 or flee the board. The detective is trying to find Jack by narrowing down suspects. Not a true 'deduction' game as it's all about process of elimination...which can be hard for both players as every character has a potential to be moved by the other player! The characters and their abilities make for tactics and replayability. There's plenty to think about and the game moves along at a nice clip.

But there there's a little disconnect with the theme as it's strange that the Jack player has no control over his/her character. An original game.

I'm a bit concerned about the set up as Ms. Swift can win on turn one if she is the Ripper. 

UPDATE: Little did I know that through some oblique twisting of the rules no one is allowed to escape on turn one.  According to Ben Vogel: As a condition for escape, there must be no witness to Jack on the preceding turn (the "Jack unseen" side of the card would need to be face up from the previous turn.) Since the setup rules specifically indicate that the witness/no witness card begins the game with the "witness" side up, there can be NO escape on turn one.  GOOD TO KNOW.

RATING: 9
This is among my favorite 2p games.  There's a surprising amount of depth, and less luck than you'd expect in this game.  There are eight investigators on the board, but one of them is the killer.  One player represents the killer, but both players move all the characters.  After four characters are moved, the Mr. Jack character announces whether the killer is in the light or dark, which allows the investigator, if he played well, to eliminate some suspects.  The main reason I think this is such a great design because the killer must take on different strategies depending on which character he represents and on the order in which character cards come up.

RATING: 8.5
Mr. Jack just broke into my top three 2-player games of all time. Yes, it was that good. While the price is up there for a 2-player game ($43 MSRP but cheaper at some stores), it is well worth it. The game is very high-quality in every way (more to come), but as good as the quality is, the gameplay and strategy steal the show. Play as Mr. Jack or the Detective. Move in and out of light and darkness according to whichever is most advantageous at the moment. Take special care to utilize the character skills wisely or you may get burned (as I have many times!) by your opponent.

The artwork immediately caught my eye. The board is incredibly detailed with a fun, cartoonish, yet realistic feel. The character and alibi "cards" can barely be called cards because of how thick and sturdy they are. The characters aren't just faceless tokens, there is character depth and storyline (bolstered by great background descriptions of each). The map itself is perfect to facilitate a balance of strategy and player advantage (with strength spots and weakness spots for each character which must be accounted for on both sides).

The gameplay is very simple in construct, but there are innumerable tactical plans which may change at a moment's notice. The entire game revolves around the witness card. If Jack is "seen" (i.e., in the light), the witness card must indicate as such which then eliminates the chance that Jack is one of the "unseen" characters, and vice versa. These characters are then tagged as innocent. This goes until either Jack escapes the city, remains hidden through the eighth round, or until the Detective makes an accurate accusation. Sound simple? Not so fast. With each player "playing" the part of two of four randomly selected characters each round, a strategy of illuminating as many characters as you can that round may be quickly thwarted by your opponents moves. Then you add the character abilities on top of that. For example, John Smith moves a streetlight (and thus the illumination it provides). Sir William Gull can switch spots with another player (got me several times last game!). Or Sherlock Holmes can eliminate an option by drawing an alibi card. I won't even get into the manholes, police cordons, or the failing streetlights. You've got to experience it for yourself!

Overall, this is one of the best 2-player games out there. It's quick (20-30 minutes), there's some luck but mostly strategy, replay value is very high, and it's a blast! I highly recommend this one and give it a solid 8.5.

RATING: 9
Sheer.  Gaming.  Brilliance!  Let the gushing now begin...  Mr. Jack is a simple game to learn yet presents an agonizing challenge to both players as they try to out-wit, out-bluff, and out-sneak one another.  And it's so well put together - I can't imagine how much play-testing went into figuring out the placement of every space and character on the board, and the details of each character's special ability.  Having said that though, the game is ever so slightly easier for the detective player than the Mr. Jack player, which means that I usually play two games at a time and switch sides with my opponent, the winner being the player who can last longer as Mr. Jack.  [Edit: with experience, it becomes easier to win as the Jack player, and it appears to be a much more balanced game than first impressions reveal.]  I don't give it a perfect 5 for enjoyment because it can become quite a brain-burner, frequently requiring a bit of waiting time while your opponent ponders all her/his options.  And I also don't give it a perfect 5 due to the minor issues of the fact that the edition I obtained was printed with a couple of small errors, and the somewhat disturbing "Jack the Ripper" theme.  My infatuation with this game is evident by the number of posts, and responses to other posts, that I have written in this game's file.  Have a read through my compiled FAQ (http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/194998) in order to answer the many questions you will have after reading the rather imperfect rules.  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 4.5/5  Total: 9/10

RATING: 7.5
[Hurrican 'Mr. Jack' 2006 edition] {Agent; deduction, angel vs devil} I am a fan of deduction games. I like games such as Sleuth, Coda, Code 777 etc.  However, it's difficult to design a good deduction game with nice interaction.  Nonetheless, Mr. Jack attracts me a lot with its theme and mechanic.  Thus, I bought it without much hesitation.  I am not disappointed.  Mr. Jack is an elegant game, which is satisfactorily designed and tuned. It is eligible to be a masterpiece of design.

Mr. Jack is a decent mix of bluffing and deduction. It's fun, engaging, interactive and thematic. The random factors prevent a solid strategy but it's tactical enough that player have a handful of decisions each turn and plan how to escape or catch.  Besides, it's highly replayable. However, it takes some time for the players to understand the power of each character.  In all, it's a very nice 2p game.

It's more difficult to be Mr. Jack; esp. for the first few games. Therefore, it's more challenging and fun to be Mr. Jack.

RATING: 8.5
Probably the best two-player-only game I know.  Very well thought-out and addictive.  It's a brain-burner, and that's what I both love and hate about it.  Like chess, it requires a fair amount of "If I go here, then my opponent will probably do this" predictions, and while satisfying as a logic puzzle, this can lead to long turn times with the wrong people.  Might be good to use chess clocks if you're playing opponents who leave time for naps between moves.  But the variety of characters and inherent randomness (Jack's identity, the witnesses who pop up on a given round, the Sherlock clues) give this a lot of replayability and make it an engaging diversion.

To the extent that this now gets significantly fewer plays than it used to. I still really like it, but often don't want to invest that amount of time working out permutations.

RATING: 6
[gameid=21763] is a deduction game with an interesting theme. The theme initially attracted us to the game and the cat'n'mouse play is fun for a while. On player takes on the role of Mr. Jack, hoping to avoid detection. The other player takes on the role of the investigator and must determine who IS Mr. Jack, before time runs out or he runs off.

You would think this would be straight up my alley. A thinking man's game, except, it isn't. I brain burn my way through the game as the investigator going back and forth, becoming more and more frustrated as the answer eludes me.

Playing as Mr. Jack is much worse, because I cannot get a grasp on how to play. Should I feint and run the other way? Bluff my way through? I have no clue how to approach it, I have no desire to work it out and I become even more frustrated at my inability to get anywhere.

I admit, I am probably not the target for this game, which is also why it has left our collection... and I know there is a good game in there - for the right people.

RATING: 5
Out of the 4 games I've played so far, I haven't seen Jack win once. I know others might consider it to be too soon to make any of the following statements based on that number of plays. Maybe our players are just too good at deduction. You start with 8 characters and that means you can deduce Jack in as little as 3 turns if the cards fall right and you know what you're doing. That depends on the luck of the draw for the characters you can move. Once you're found out, it's over because there's no place on the board you can really run away and hide because of the sewer movement.

So the whole game comes down to trying to choose roles to move tokens in such a way that you remove as much of an influence from your opponent as possible. Both players are trying to do that, so who wins depends on luck of the draw. That's fun for the first few times playing, but then things start to become clear on what's going on and it becomes old.

It seems the best technique for Jack is to cluster everyone together and wait for the 8 turns to pass. Mostly you need to have the card of the person you want to remove from the light. It takes too many actions to remove all the tokens and lamplights from around them. It's easier to remove them directly, but that depends on luck. You can easily put people back in the light with almost any card. You can move next to them, shine a light on them, swap spots with them, make them come running to you. So it seems that the investigator wants to cut the remaining suspects in half and push people in the dark and Jack wants to hang out with everyone under a lamplight until sun up.

RATING: 7
Mr. Jack is a lovely little two-player deduction game. The components are nice and the atmosphere adds a lot to gameplay. For some reason, every time I play I make a small little mistake that costs me the game. I say this because the strategy at first seems deceptively easy, but you have to stay alert to all the details on the board. One wrong move and your opponent sweeps in to claim victory. I initially had rated this lower, but once I discovered the strategy was more complex than I realized, I became rather addicted to this game--especially because I rarely ever win! I'll get the hang of it one day; until then, it's just as much fun losing.

RATING: 5
London detectives versus Jack the Ripper!
Jack is trying to escape the city but must remain incognito to do so. The detective is organizing a search party and is trying to narrow down who amongst the area's people is actually Jack.

Uses a line-of-sight mechanic to determine who can or cannot see Jack, and the players must logic out which of the characters (that they both have a chance to control) is the murderer.

Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 2
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 3
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 1
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 3


Overall - 2

RATING: 8
This game deserves merit for the attempt at what it is but there was not enough good effort in actually trying to make it a functional game.  This game is way too lopsided to be fun.  Play Jack and you have get to run around hoping you don't make one minor mistake.  Play the detectives and you get idly laze about, half paying attention and eventually be handed the victory.  The various characters are great with their own individual effects on the game, very keen idea and certainly that's where the game lies but it's not enough to make this something that stands out.  There's needs to be some sort of balancing mechanic or system that allows the Jack player to maybe have more control over which characters move.  Not sure how this one would be fixed but it's just not what is should be as it is.

UPDATE: After a few more plays and including the expansion characters and the alternate starting position I've really changed my mind on this game. It's a lot of fun now (granted there were many changes to make it so) and I really get a kick out of going through this one now.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

This is a clever little deduction game where the main objective is to force the murderer to split the characters into revealed (in the light or next to somone) or hidden. Every turn the murderer must tell you if his character is revealed or hidden. Then the players move two characters and employ their special abilities. The asymmetric nature of the player abilities makes for some interesting choices. It's easier to stay revealed early on, but lights start going out as the night wears on, and if the murderer ever starts the turn hidden, he can make a dash for one of the exits.

The game is pretty fun. Initially it seemed a little stacked in favor of the detective, but I think with good play you can keep the detective puzzling over two or three characters until the last round. At which point it's in the detective's best interest to randomly accuse one of the characters left.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
One of the two players represents Jack the Ripper, who will be one of the 8 characters on the board. This player knows the identity of this character and his goal is to flee from the district as soon as possible (or avoid being accused for eight turns). The other player represents an independent investigator (not represented on the board) who tries to guess the identity of Jack. But he can make only one accusation during the game!

During each turn the players move the characters, using their special powers, placing them either in shadow or light. At the end of each turn, the witnesses declare if Jack is visible (in light, or adjacent to another character) or not (alone in the shadows). This allows the investigator to know which characters are innocent. This continues as the investigator tries to eliminate suspects while Jack tries to escape. Intuition, logic and cold blood will be necessary for each of the two participants.

RATING: 5
Wow, what a fun little game! I usually go for heavier stuff, mostly wargames, but this seems like a really excellently-designed light game. Everything just "fits" in terms of the characters' abilities, the flow of the game, and the components. Definitely a find in the filler game category. It's worth noting that the game doesn't really play out like a "deduction" game a la Clue, despite the theme. The gameplay is much more tactical in nature - how can the investigator split suspects between light and dark, and how can Jack foil those plans?

Update: Still fun, but not quite worth the hype it gets around here, IMO. The game develops a certain "sameness" after a few plays - while the card draws enforce some variety, you don't really approach the game with any new insights after the first few outings. I'll stick with my "7" on this one.

Update 2: Haven't pulled this out in years, and don't miss it at all. Dropped to a 5.
