RATING: 7
This is a nifty design, and has some elements that will draw in players who aren't keen on deduction games.  While deducing who Jack is is a central part of the game, it's just as important to know which character to use on your turn, and how to manipulate the board to either hide from the police, or locate Jack.  It seems to be very easy to deduce who Jack is, at least by the fourth turn, and it quickly develops into a game of cat-and-mouse, but the game plays quickly, and offers a nice, tasty challenge.  I only wonder if the games will become fairly repetitious over time.

5 plays: 2 players

Extension

RATING: N/A
One of the two players represents Jack the Ripper, who will be one of the 8 characters on the board. This player knows the identity of this character and his goal is to flee from the district as soon as possible (or avoid being accused for eight turns). The other player represents an independent investigator (not represented on the board) who tries to guess the identity of Jack. But he can make only one accusation during the game!
\13\\13\
During each turn the players move the characters, using their special powers, placing them either in shadow or light. At the end of each turn, the witnesses declare if Jack is visible (in light, or adjacent to another character) or not (alone in the shadows). This allows the investigator to know which characters are innocent. This continues as the investigator tries to eliminate suspects while Jack tries to escape. Intuition, logic and cold blood will be necessary for each of the two participants.

RATING: 8
Interesting game. I rate after one play and revise later if my opinion changes, but usually I can tell if a game is likely to rise or fall after more plays. With this one, I could see it going either way. The level of randomness seems like it could doom this one for me (especially as I'm a fan of 2-player Scotland Yard, which scratches the same itch with no randomness after the setup). On the other hand, figuring out how to best use each character's ability seems like it might lend a nice level of depth to the experience, a big plus in a game with this short of playing time. One thing I can definitely say is that I was favorably impressed with the components, and would not hesitate to buy another game from Hurrican.

RATING: 10
I love two player games where the players have different goals, and I love games where each character has a special ability (see: Lord of the Rings: The Confrontation, Heroscape)--thus, Mr. Jack was a no-brainer for me.  The game art is among my very favorites.  People that complain about the lack of deduction in the deduction element are kind of missing the point.  It's not really a deduction game in the usual sense.  If you think of the number of revealed players as a scoring track, Jack is trying to keep the marker on one end, while the detective is trying to move that marker to the other end.  Anyway, we'll see how this holds up after a lot of plays, but right now I'm excited about it.

RATING: 9
A nearly perfect game- short, challenging, and varied. The beauty lies in the fact that the strategies of the Investigator and Jack are so different although they both use the same characters turn after turn, which themselves have cleverly varied powers. The only issue lies in small loopholes and shortfalls, such as Watson's relative uselessness, or Sherlock, Ms. Stealthy, or Goodley's slight overpoweredness. All in all, one of the greatest games I have played and one I would recommend to anyone, beginner or expert.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
It is very rare for me to research a game so thoroughly before purchasing it to only wind up detesting it after a few plays.  Mr. Jack is theorectically a good game, yet I would have to disagree wholeheartedly.

After playing two sessions, I was left VERY unfulfilled.  Not only did I feel the game was laughably unbalanced, but there was no way the Jack player could ever make it to turn 8 without being uncovered or accused... yet alone escape!  Unless the inspector is not very bright or extremely unlucky, Mr. Jack has NO chance of winning due to strategy.  It is ALL luck!  

I played nine sessions total as Jack and in the end won once due to simple luck - the conditions were set up perfectly for me to escape.  I thought maybe my "strategy" was flawed and gave the inspector side a try and found I could even not pay attention and still win! 

I am not at all whining... I am simply stating my perception of a game that I really wanted to like.  I love the theme yet this really falls short on all accounts.  I understand that the dark theme would make some people uncomfortable, but that is no excuse to bubble it up with cartoon renditions.  Simply put, the artwork does not match the theme whatsoever.

Some of the components such as the game board and the character pieces are just nice, but for the price of the game, the quality is significantly lacking.  The character and alibi cards are way too thick and show wear just after a few plays... and I take excesively good care of my games at all times!

I do understand that I am a minority in that I am one of few who didn't find Mr. Jack loads of fun, but I think I gave this game many chances to justify the pumped up reviews it got here.
